Data for individual sampling points from the outer disks (r>r25) from Bigiel et al. (2010)
column 1: log10 HI surface density at sampling point [log(Msun/pc2)]
column 2: log10 SFR surface density at sampling point [log(Msun/yr/kpc2)]
Uncertainties:
1) HI: sensitivity ~ 0.4 Msun/pc2, calibration uncertainty ~10%.
2) SFR(FUV): sensitivity ~ 2*10^-5 Msun/yr/kpc^2, uncertainty ~ 7*10^-6 Msun/yr/kpc^2. To convert FUV intensities into SFR surface densities: calibration uncertainty ~50%, but covariant within a galaxy (from comparison with other tracers). 
Notes:
1) Contrary to the paper, a factor of 1.36 to acount for helium is included in the HI surface densities.
2) The data were sampled at a common angular resolution of 15 arcsec.
3) Note that many of the SFR (FUV) data are below the sensitivity used in Bigiel et al. (2010). It is thus especially important to pay attention to averaging and uncertainties when using these data.
4) Surface densities are corrected to account for inclination.
5) The SFR surface densities are directly proportional to far UV intensity. The calibration assumes a Chabrier IMF.
6) Data points are roughly independent, but slight oversampling does occur in some regions.
References:
1) Sampling points and this result: Bigiel et al. (2010)
2) HI Maps: THINGS, Walter et al. (2008)
3) Galaxy Distance and Orientation: Walter et al. (2008)
4) SFR Maps: GALEX far UV (Gil de Paz et al. 2007, Salim et al. 2007)
